DEVIANTLY HAVE A PRODUCT WITH SALVADOR ALDEREGUIA (SA),

HAS NO OBJECT ON TO THE PROCESS. THE REA TO S-1 THAT RACTIION HAS NO INTEREST
ALSO SHOULD WAKE IT CLEAR TO S-1 THAT RACTIION HAS NO INTEREST
C IN HIS (S-1'S) CONTINUED RELATIONSHIP.

PACHANKIS CURRENTLY IN ACTIVATED RACTI, INDICATES THAT VNCANOPY
APPROXIMATE TO THE EFFECT ON EACH CASE, WITH THE
APPREYPTION OF DEFECTORS SUCH AS SLANK-1 WHO HAD BEEN HANDED
AS A DEFECTOR ALTHOUGH ACCORDING TO THE FILE HE NEVER OFFICIALLY
GRANTED THIS STATUS UNDER PL 110. MOS DOES NOT CODORJNATE
EACH INDIVIDUAL MEETING NOR IDENTIFY OFFICER HANDLING CASE
TO VNCANOPY.

CIR-317 / 01514-78

RESF: A. FBI TELETYPE PATED 0520262 APRIL 1978, CAPTIONED AS
ABOVE
6. CIR-316/00260-75, DATED 18 FEBRUARY 1975, CAPTIONED
S.ALVAODAR ALDEREGUIA, ALSO KNOWN AS "EL GALLEGO" INTERNAL SECURITY-
CUBA: 1: WITH REGARD TO CLARIFICATION OF SALVADOR ALDEREGUIA'S
ASSOCIATION WITH J.S. GOVERNMENT AGENCIES AND PARTICULARLY WITH CIA,
REFECTIONE B ADVISED THAT ME WAS OF INTEREST TO THIS AGENCY IN 1960
WHEN FEBRUARY 1975, CIR-316/00260-75, DATED 18 FEBRUARY 1975,
FROM CUBA, HOWEVER, HE TOOK ASYLON IN ASSISTING IN HIS EXFILTRATION
HAVANA ON 3 JULY 1960 AND DEPARTED THE SAME DAY FOR CURACAO. AFTER
HIS ARRIVAL IN MIAMI IN FEBRUARY 1961, THIS AGENCY WAS BRIEFLY IN
CARTIC WITH MIIM BUT OUR INTEREST WAS DROPPED PARTLY BECAUSE HIS
UNCLE IN THE 1960-1961 CONDURERS OF THE CUBAN COMMUNIST PARTY, WAS
INCELATIVE AMBASSADOR TO VOLASTIA AND ALDEREGUIA'S TRUE LOYALTIES
THEN UNKNOWN. THIS AGENCY HAS HAD NO INTEREST. IN OR CONTACT WITH
ALDEREGUIA SINCE THAT TIME, THE CUBA AND THE CUBA COMPANY 1937,
HAWANA, CUBA NAS A FORMER DGI STAFF OFFICER WHO DETECTED ON 21
APRIL 1964 IN HILFAXY WOS COTIA. HE WAS DEBRIEFED AND MANOLED
THROUGH NORMAL DEFECTOR CHANNELS AND WAS THE SOURCE OF UNDEROUS
CSC1'S CONCERNING THE OGI IN 1964 AND 65. HE WAS USED OPERATIONALLY
IN THE 1964-1964 TETMPTS AGAINST DGI OFFICERS
OURING 1964-1964 TO THE CUBA AND THE CUBA.
JULY 1967, AND WAS CONSIDERED, BUT NEVER USED, FOR ANOTHER
RECRUITMENT ATTEMPT IN 1971. SINCE 1971 RORDRIGUEZ HAS NOT BEEN
INVOLVED IN ANY CIA OPERATION IN MIAMI OR ELSEWHERE.
JOSEPH NORRIS IS THE ALIAS OF A
CIA REPRESENTATIVE WHO PERIODICALLY DEBRIERS RODRIGUEZ ON PERSONALITE
AND METHODS OF THE DGI. THERE IS NO OTHER CIA INVOLVEMENT WITH
RODRIGUEZ.
3. THIS AGENCY WILL QUERY ITS REPRESENTATIVE IN MIAMI TO
DETERMININE IF HE HAS ANY ADDITIONAL INFORMATION RELEVANT TO THIS
MATTER.
Slypen

SECRET
MEMORANDUM OF ORAL COMMITMENT
SUBJECT: Engagement of SLANK-1 (201-749651)
1. Term and Project Charge: Subject has been engaged
under oral contract for use under Project SLEEPER. The
effective date of the oral contract is 16 Oct 1975.
2. Security Approval: An OA for the operational use of
Subject outside the U.S. was granted on 6 Jan 1971.
3. Citizenship: Subject is a United States Citizen.
4. Compensation: Subject is reimbursed for travel expenses
and is given a salary replacement for any time he is required
to be assent form work at the request of the Agency. The
amount of investment will not exceed $40 a day. He may be
awarded cash for taxes for services rendered. He may also
be given gifts for time to time, the individual value
of which will not exceed $50.
5. Taxes: Subject is obligated to pay U.S. taxes and
should be issued a Revised Facility Form 1099 at the end
of each tax year.
6. Quarters and/or Subsistence:
a. Subject is not furnished quarters or subsistence.
b. No commitments have been made regarding additional
compensation to accommodate increased cost of living and
quarters expenses.
7. Operational Expenses: Subject will be reimbursed for
operational expenses such as entertainment of operational
contacts, phone calls, cover expenses, etc., upon
submission of proper accounting for such expenses.

8. Contingent Obligations Although no commitment to
this effect has been made to Subject, should the security
of Subject or his family become threatened because of
activities undertaken by him at the request of this
Agency, this Agency would have an obligation to reimburse
Subject for expenses required to reduce that threat,
including expenses needed to relocate Subject and his
family and if necessary, to supplement his income while
he is establishing a new residence and employment.
9. No commitments other than those stated above have
been made to Subject.

JUAN is
21 December 1974
SUBJECT: Contact Report on SLAIK-1. (S-1)
1. S-1 was met on the afternoon of 21 December, for ahrief social
call, to pay our reponents and present him with a bottle of
Scotch for the Christmas season.
2. S-1 was grateful not only for the gift but to see we had not
forgotten him. His home life seems to have settled down after
some rocky periods earlier in the year and he has a new, more
secure position as bus discover for the Metro Cransit Authority
here in Miami. was mostly reported, he has also taken that
postal Services and would accepted a letter carrier's job
if it is offered to him.
3. As always, 3-1 is ready to assist us in any way that he can.
If Hoberto, RORRIBEL Lilmpurt should over come out again, S-1
can be noted on to make an approach. All that we would have
be is to contact his employers and obtain the necessary
commission.
Henry 3. PAGKINKIS.

B. SLALOM-1 - He is close to Nestor RANIREZ,
a CURAPESCA Representative who is currently in Tokyo.
SLALOM-1 states RANIREZ is approachable because RANIREZ
is definitely not a Consunist, and he thinks very much
like him (SLALOM-1).
C. SLANK-1 He mentioned to PACIANKIS that
he had been close to Roberto RODRIGUEZ Lompart, a Cuban
Mining Official who often travels to Mexico and Canada.
D. Gustavo MAS - Brother-in-law of the current
Cuban Ambassador to Mexico. MAS has advised PACIANKIS
that he is willing to help us only to the extent of
determining the feelings of his sister and the Ambassador
at any given time, but no more. He will not accept any
remuneration from us and will foot his own bill to visit
his sister.
E. SICOOL-1 and SLACK-1 -- In describing the
former, PACIANKIS referred to him as from another
generation, i.c., of the ROA class, who could possibly
be used with any older Cuban officials that night still
be around. He cautioned however, that SICOOL-1 had
undergone a delicate center operation. He was a
conformant to the American Association. As concern SLACK-1,
PACHANKIS suggested that we were probably better off
forgetting him. lie described SLACK-1 as very problematical
and then went on to add such adjectives as avaricious,
sly, secretive, and a person inclined not to follow-
through on any task given him.
6. PACIANKIS believes that much can be done with
the above defectors against the targets mentioned and,
himself, is anxious to get involved in another recruitment
operation as soon as possible.
Frank C. Esquivel

2d Scasima
REPORT
No. 92-880
VLADIMIR RODRIGUEZ LAHERA
JUSKE 19, 1972 - Ordered to be pristed
Mr. ENSTLAND, from the Committee on the Judiciary,
submitted the following
REPORT
[To accompany H.R. 2078]
The Committee on the Judiciary, to which, was referred the bill
(H.R. 2076) for the relief of Vladimir Rodriguez LAHERA, having
considered the same, reports favorably thereon without amendment
and recommends that the bill do pass.
FURPOSE OF THE BILL.
The purpose of the bill is to enable Vladimir Rodriguez LAHER
to file a petition for naturalization, notwithstanding the fact that he
was formerly a member of a proscribed organization.
The board of the bill is not a member of a committee.
The beneficiary of the bill is a 25-year-old native and citizen of Cuba,
whose status was adjusted to that of a lawful resident alien on No-
vember 2, 1986, retroactive to April 20, 1984, the data on which he was
awarded to the public, and the majority of the parties in Miami, Fla.,
with his wife, a lawful resident alien, and two domesticers of the
ficiary was employed in Cuba with the General Directorate of Intelli-
ance and served in the Cuban Hotel Army. Without enactment of
the public the beneficiary would be unable to petition for naturalization
until 1976.

that 'K o D R I G U E Z 2. is under the control of any, hostile
intelligence service.
3. The psychiatric and periodic medical examinations have
shown that & O D R I G U E Z has no serious radical or psychiatric

EXCERPT FROM JOURNAL
OFFICE OF LEGISLATIVE COUNSEL
Thursday - 24 February 1972
3. (Confidential - JGO) Met with Mr. Garner J. Cline, Counsel,
Subcommittee No. 1. House Judiciary Committee, who told me that there would
be no problem with the Democratic objector relating to H, R. 2076, a bill for
the relief of Vladimir Rodriguez LAHERA. Mr. Donald Benn, Associate Counsel
of the Judiciary Committee, has not touched base as yet with the Republican
objector but will do. so before the private calendar is called on 7 March.
Mr. Eline told the also that the Davis bill, K. R. 5176 was 'normally
labled by the Nll Committee in id' meeting of 22 February. The tabring was
without discusain on the basis of the adverse recommendation by the Subcommittee.
See Memg for Record dated 11 February 1972 on A Trevor Gallehex.

OFFICE OF LEGISLATIVE COUNSEL
3. (Confidential - JGO) Met with Mr. Drury Blair, Senate Immigration
and Naturalization Subcommittee staff, who told me that due to the primaries
in the Chairman's home state he did not believe that any further meetings of the
Subcommittee will be held until mid June. H. R. 2076, a bill for the relief
of Vladimir Rodriguez LAHera, is on the agenda for the next Subcommittee
meeting. Miss Chris Hopkins, WH Division, has been advised.

DCC-MICRO-SEA
MORTGUM
SAINT
TYPIC/Future Use of AMBUC-1
JUL 151911
ACTION EXPIRES EMFERENCES
MICROFILMED
Action Required: FYI
1. During JKLANCE's most recent attempt to contact
AMETROPIA-1 via AMBUC-1, it became readily apparent that
the cover story AMBUC-1 utilized with his immediate
superior was unsatisfactory from two points: First, it
did not permit us the operational flexibility so necessary
in an approach of this sort and secondly, if AMBUC-1 had
been advanced when he did, his job security would have been
jeopardized.
2. To correct the above deficiency, WII/Miami has
arranged the following with the Miami Field Office (MFO):
In the future, if we again utilize AMBUC-1 to approach a
PUBLICATION official, we will ask that the MFO arrange to have
been given to the MFO. We will not have a number of
component contact the appropriate senior official of
AMMUG-1's company. This senior official will in turn
notify AMMUG-1's immediate superior that AMBUC-1 is to be
permitted to travel on matters of importance to the
Department of Defense.
3. Transmitted under separate cover is a copy of
a memorandum we received from the MFO concerning the above
arrangements.
Eustace D. KLOOK
Attachment:
Memo, u/s/c via True Name Pouch
Distribution:
3 - C/WID w/att u/s/c

21 JUNE 1971

3 June 1971
MEMORANDUM FOR : Chief of Station, WH/Miami
FROM
: MFO
ATTENTION
: Security Officer
SUBJECT
: Ralph. MOSEDA
1. Reference your memorandum OS 169-71.
2. Pursuant to your request this office contacted a senior
official of the Marriott Corporation in Washington, D.C., who
approved the travel to Europe of a Miami barred Marriott employee
who is affiliated with WH.
3. The Marriott official, Mr. James McALLISTER,
contacted his Miami representation, Mr. Ralph ICSEDA, and
advised NOSEDA that your asset was free to travel to Spain on short
notice.
4. NCSEDA was advised by MEALLISTER that this was a matter
of interest to the Department of Defense. NCSEDA, to the best of our
knowledge, has not been approached by anyone else in Miami or Washington
on this matter since the initial call from M-ALLISTER in March.
cist
REUBED: O. HARVELL
DOC. MICRO. SER.

C.AN JUNO G INIZING
FROM
Chief of Station, WILMAMM
DISTRIBUTION
MISTY
Mist of U.S. Immigration Official to AMMUG-1
ACTION REGIONS
ACTION REQUIRED: None, FYI only.
1. During the 'undersigned's most recent meeting with
AMMUG-1, the agent stated that a Mr. Rex M. G r i f f i n, an
investigator of the U.S. Immigration and Naturalization Service
(INS) had visited him on 13 April 1971. According to AMMUG-1,
the purpose of Griffin's visit was to inquire into AMMUG-1's
present welfare and the 100% his relationship to
the American Government. Mr. J. H. O. Soror of
H.R. #2076 which will expedite AMMUG-1's application for U.S.
citizenship by waiving the standard waiting period.) When asked
about his relationship with Mr. Rodino, AMMUG-1 simply explained
that Mr. Rodino was a friend of his from Washington.
2. Griffin explained that the reason that he wanted to
talk to AMMUG-1 personally, was the fact that nearly all of the
information surrounding AMMUG-1 was hold in INS: office in
Washington. Mr. J. H. O. Soror information that was held by the
Miami office was closely held in access to the files was
severely restricted. During his visit, Griffin asked AMMUG-1 if
he noticed any unusual interest in his comments and goings, to
which AMMUG-1 replied negatively.
3. In view of above, believe it reasonable to assume that
Griffin suspects that JKLANCE is somehow involved with AMMUG-1.
This position is concurred in by Station Officer who maintains
liaison with the Miami office of the INS.
4. AMMUG-1 characterized Mr. Griffin's visit as being
very pleasant and commented that he was "my unable". In sum,
there does not appear to be any need for intervention on
AMMUG-1's behalf or on that of the Station. If the need does
arise, we will promptly inform Headquarters.
DISTRIBUTION:
3 - C/WHD
CROAT RESEARCH TO

DATT

COC
CONTACT REPORT
CASE OFFICER: Eustace D. KLOOCK
AGENT: AMMUG-1
PLACE: AMMUG-1's home
DATE/TIME: 6 April 1971 1530-1800
1. On 6 April 1971 I reviewed with AMMUG-1, Volume I
of the Cuban mugbooks. He identified the individuals listed
in para 2 below. Un less otherwise noted, the following
general comments apply to all: That he knew them quite
well and the last time he saw them was 1963-1964, usually in
Mexican region.
2. Arsenic FRANCO Villanueva (201-346425). According
to AMMUG-1, FRANCO is G-2, and is one of the individuals he
approached (at our behest) during the Pan American games
which were held in Puerto Rico in 1966. He commented that
FRANCO dismissed AMMUG-1's initial approach out of hand
stating that he was a Marxist-Leninist. According to AMMUG-1,
while a follow up was supposed to be made in Caguas, Puerto
 Rico, the staff officer who was accompanying AMMUG-1 decided
against it.
Jorge E. GARCIA-BANGO Dírube (201-736492). AMMUG-1
commented that GARCIA-BANGO was the other individual that
he tried to approach during the Pan American games. Like
FRANCO above, while a follow up was planned for Caguas,
Puerto Rico, the staff officer accompanying AMMUG-1 decided
against it.
Cic Culang
Ecllo LOBAINA Lobaina. AMMUG-1 commented that he
did not know LOBAINA very well. He added that he used to
be AMMUG-1's instructor in firearms at the Police Academy.

MIRFORTUM
TYPIC/Cuban Mughook
ACTION REQUIRED - REFERENCES
REFERENCE: UFAA-2768, 1 March 1971
1. Your request to show the Cuban Mugbooks, Volumes I and II,
to AMCARD-1 and AMMUG-1 is approved.
2. Per Reference, paragraph 2, Headquarters will forward
such photographs of Cuban officials to WH/Miami.
3. We are planning a slight change in the new Cuban Mug-
book (Volume III). This Mugbook will be distributed earlier (i.e.,
after 100 photos have been collected rather than after 500 as was
of the case with Volume II) and in looseleaf binders. As new sections
of the Volume III are compiled, probably in groups of 100 photos,
the following text to the Stations concerned to be added to Volume
III. Incidentally, as a result of your comment on the most recent
Mugbook, we are making an alphabetical listing for Volume II to
the Stations which received this Mugbook.
Thornton V. CARUANA
Distribution:
3 - COS, WH/Miami
CO

CITYIC:Cuban Mugbook
ACTION REQUIRED REFRESHIS
1. Request permission to show AUCARD-1 and
AUCIU-1 Cuban mugbooks, Volume I and II.
2. We have noted that on a number of occasions
in the past, photographs of Cuba officials which
have been obtained by our various Stations abroad,
are generally sent only to Headquarters. We request
that when Headquarters does receive such photographs
that WH/Miami be provided with a copy. It should
be borne in mind that barring overriding security
considerations, it is our intention to know such
prototypes to AUCARD-1 and AMCA-1 to possible
identification.
